Mr Smith/ Mr. Dinar

| received a public notice for an upcoming meeting on 616 South B Street, the 48 unit
apartment complex.

For the last five years, | have owned a condominium at 808 Laurel, literally a 5 minute
walk from the proposed building. Our complex is 36 units, including 13 rentals. It's not
an especially high income building, with selling prices in the $650-865K range. Our
residents are composed of a wide demographic. We have teachers, health care
professionals, Silicon Valley techies, retirees, etc. Workplaces are all over the place,
including many currently working from home.

| am on the HOA board. Our building has 36 parking spots for the 36 units. | know
each resident fairly well, and know that in total, our residents have 50 vehicles, 36
parked in the garage, and 14 on the street. That is a 39% overage to the street. | would
bet that ratio holds right through the neighborhood, since the parking situation is
ridiculous and the city has always been lax about the 72 hour parking rule, especially
during COVID.


--- page 177 ---
3
 
Our experience with renters in the building is that more people on average, compared to 
owned units, occupy the units to afford them.  Of the 13 renters, they have a total of 21 
cars, a 62% overage with 8 cars on the street. 
 
As far as I know, only one couple in the building bikes or takes the train to work.  
 
I attended planning meetings for a large building about to be constructed along the 
tracks.There was less than one parking spot per unit in that building proposal.  Planners 
have this idea that since the units are close to the train, people will take public transport, 
bike or walk.   That is rubbish.The train is very expensive and doesn't service the key 
business areas in San Fran, as well as Silicon Valley High tech.  Have you taken the 
train into San Fran, planning to get to the financial district or downtown? 
 
I used to work in high tech and commuted to Sunnyvale every day.  It was still better to 
drive that horrible traffic than attempt it via public transport and multiple connections.  If 
everyone worked in downtown San Fran, I get it, but they don't. Further, it's pretty much 
a requirement  to have a car to pick up groceries, and most other services if you live in 
the downtown area. 
 
If the 808 Laurel experience holds, the 48 proposed apartments could lead to a low of 
67 cars (50/36*48) or possibly up to 77 cars (21/13*48) using our rental numbers. 
 
With all the buildings planned for the area, how many of these proposed new residents 
will be looking for parking spots on the San Mateo downtown streets (and competing 
with the needs of our merchants)? 
 
I'm fine with more apartments/condos in the downtown core. Just ensure they are built 
with parking spaces based on reality, not some planning fantasy or false cost saving 
measure. 
 
Thank you, 
David Rubinfeld

Dear Mr. Smith: 
 
Pursuant to the Public Notice regarding Neighborhood Meeting on PA‐2021‐036, I am submitting comments 
on behalf of the Stradbally Court Home Owners Association. Stradbally Court is located at 222 6th Avenue in 
San Mateo,  abutting the two commercial structures that are going to be demolished in this proposed project. 
The proposed new five story mixed use building will be right next door to us. 
 
Please see the attached for our comments, expressing some of our concerns regarding this proposed project. 
 
If you need to contact us, please call Beth Chang at 
 or Catherine Lau at 
. 
 
Thank you for your consideration. 
 
Stradbally Court HOA

--- page 179 ---
Comments regarding 616 S. B  Street, San Mateo 
 
1. How many parking spaces are available in the 
proposed garage? With 48 apartment units plus 
commercial suites, there should be enough parking 
for the residents and visitors/customers so as not to 
add to the parking congestion on 6th street. 
2.  Where will the driveway into the garage be located?  
We would propose, for the developer’s 
consideration, that the driveway into their garage be 
aligned parallely to the side yard of Stradbally Court 
(by the Maple trees), running perpendicular to 6th 
Avenue, with the entrance to the garage on 6th 
Avenue. Locating the driveway as proposed above 
accomplishes three objectives which are mutually 
beneficial. 
(a)  This will provide more open space between the 
2 buildings so that natural light can be 
maximized for both buildings. 
(b) Increased space between the 2 buildings will 
also minimize the possible risk of damaging 
Stradbally Court’s foundation especially since 
the proposed building features an underground 
parking garage. In view of what happened in 
Florida’s condo collapse, one cannot dismiss 
such consideration.

--- page 180 ---
(c) Residents of both buildings would not be 
looking into each other’s windows, thereby, 
increasing privacy . 
3. The residents of Stradbally Court would like the 
Maple trees that are currently on (and adjacent to) 
the property line between Stradbally Court and Tap 
Plastics be preserved and not be cut down. That 
would provide further screening between the two 
buildings and increase “green” appeal and natural 
landscaping. Should the tress get damaged or killed 
during construction, they should be replaced by 
trees of same size and height to preserve green 
space and privacy. 
4.  If at all possible the windows facing Stradbally Court 
should be staggered so that residents of the two 
buildings will not be looking into each other’s 
windows. 
5.  The developer is urged to consider a design that 
sees the building taper upwards. In other words, the 
upper floors are set back further than the lower 
floors. This tapered design has the advantage of 
increasing natural light as well as minimizing a wind 
tunnel effect between the buildings. 
6.   Are the recreational and common areas on the first, 
second and fifth floors of the proposed building 
outdoors or indoors? If they are outdoors, there

--- page 181 ---
should be noise mitigation measures taken. For 
example, raucous noises from a basketball game 
would be very disturbing to the neighbors.

(616 S. B Street, San Mateo, CA 94401 APN-034194-030)

Dear Sir/Madam:

| am the President of the Stradbally Court Condominium Homeowners
Association. The condominium | represent is located at 222 6" Avenue
and we would be the immediate neighbor of the proposed Nazareth
Vista building on 616 S. B Street.

We attended the neighborhood Meeting held on January 20, 2022
concerning the Nazareth Vista Pre-Application to build a 95,820 square-
foot, mix use building. The plans submitted by the project’s Architect,
Mr. Dinah, demonstrated consideration and mindfulness of light and
the feeling of openness for the neighbors. We greatly appreciate these
nice touches. However, we do have a couple of concerns. Before the
January 20 meeting, we submitted written comments, detailing our



--- page 183 ---
concerns and during the meeting, Mr. Dinah said he will respond but to
date, we have not received anything.

In brief, there are two vital concerns which we would like to bring to
the attention of the Planning Commission, from the perspective of
Stradbally Court and the other communities on 6" Avenue.

Currently, there is a grove of 5 Maple trees, several of which could be
considered Heritage trees, on the NW side of the proposed building site
that we believe should be preserved. This grove of trees is truly
beautiful and is a natural asset of this section of 6 Avenue (our
neighborhood). It also serves as a natural screen between our building
and the new building. That is actually a win-win situation since the
residents of the two buildings would not be looking into their
neighbors’ homes but a naturally green view. To cut them down to
make additional space for an apartment building would be killing a
“green” gift that took at least twenty years to mature and develop.
We, therefore, ask that the Planning Commission to only approve an
architectural plan that preserves this grove of trees from being cut-
down. Weare not architects nor city planners, but we have attached a
rough plot of the trees as enclosures (1 and 2). As far as we can glean
from the Plans, this area appears to be a parking area. We believe that
parking spaces can be arranged around the trees.

The second issue involves set-backs from the pedestrian sidewalk. On
this section of 6" Avenue (between Laurel and S. B Street), the setback
of all the buildings is between 15 and 20 feet. See the architectural
plans for: (1) The Stratford (601 Laurel Street), (2) The Stradbally Court
(222 6 Avenue); and (3) Gramercy On the Park (555 Laurel Street). See
also enclosures 3-5. It would seem incongruous for The Nazareth

Vista to have a building footprint that extends to the current sidewalk ,
which contravenes our established community setbacks. It would ruin
the look and feel of this section of 6th Avenue. Therefore, we think



--- page 184 ---
that Nazareth Vista should have an equal setback to that of The
Stradbally Court and The Stratford Assisted Living Condominiums. The
Nazareth Vistas plans should conform to the established character of
our neighborhood. We hereby provide pictures of the relevant aspects
of 6" Avenue to show that all the buildings in this neighborhood have
15-20 setbacks. We urge the Commission to consider asking the
Developer to modify the plans accordingly.

We would be very happy to discuss this with the Commission. Please

contact re 2 aaa

Warmest regards,
Beth H. Chang
President, Stradbally Court Condominium Homeowners’ Association

GUMBINGER

AVR IN M February 1*, 2022

City of San Mateo Planning Commission
ARCHITECTS 330 W. 20th Ave.,
San Mateo, CA 94403

Re: 6165S. B Street/ Proposed Nazareth Vista
Mixed Use Development
6" Street front Setback

Dear Planning Commissioners;

I have reviewed the current Project Plans as of November 16, 2021, posted on the
City's website and offer my comments below.

In my opinion, the proposed project will provide relief from needed housing,
additional commercial spaces, consistency facing B street where the facade of the
building aligns with other commercial buildings as well as a nice articulation of
the street view frontages.

It is in this context, that I would like to bring to the attention of the
Commissioners, the absence of front setback of the proposed Nazareth Vista
building on 6" street, that differs from the relationship of the existing adjacent and
surrounding buildings: Stradbally Court, Gramercy on the Park and Stratford,
which comply with a minimum of 15 feet setback.

The existing open space, landscaped, setbacks on both sides of 6th street from
South B St to Laurel provide a strong and visual connection to Central Park, a
neighborhood and Downtown San Mateo asset.

In my opinion and to the best of my knowledge, information and belief, the
relationship of a building to its surroundings is of greater importance than the
individual structure.

With this last paragraph in mind, respectfully I urge the Planning Commissioners
to request a revision/adjustment to the Nazareth Vista plans to provide a minimum
of 15 feet frontage setback facing 6" Street.

Very truly yours,
Gumbinger Ayram Architects, Inc.

~ Noemi K. Avram, AIA
President

To: Planning Commission members:  
 
I am a resident of The Stratford at 601 Laurel Avenue. The Stratford is an 11-story Senior Living Condominium 
for 80 residents. I am President of our Home Owners’ Association. Our residents have moved here to enjoy 
living in the friendly environment of this neighborhood. From our east side windows, balconies, and patio, we 
have beautiful views of trees, the Bay, East Bay hills and the San Mateo Bridge.  
 
The addition of the proposed five-story residential/commercial building at 616 S. B St. will cause an unwelcome 
change to our neighborhood:  
 
Major loss of the view from the east side of our building. 
 
More traffic on 6th & 7th and B St. 
 
Less street parking for our visitors and staff. 
 
The proposed large “block” building creates a wall blocking our and others’ views. 
Therefore, I would propose/suggest that the height of the building be reduced from five stories to four stories to 
lessen the disruption to our neighborhood.  
 
Also, that the rooftop be designed to attractively screen off the view of any mechanical equipment by adding a 
professionally designed rooftop garden.  
 
We would appreciate that consideration be given to these requests.  
 
Carol Ruiter  
601 Laurel Ave
  
San Mateo, CA 94401

--- page 195 ---
February 3, 2022 THE STRATFORD

Reference PA-2021-036
6168S. B St. Nazareth Vista

To Somer Smith, AICP, Associate Planner,

I am writing to you on behalf The Stratford residents at 601 Laurel Avenue. The Stratford is a
boutique, luxury high-rise senior living community with over 70 residents. As the new
development progresses and the negative impacts it will have on our residents and neighborhood
become apparent several important issues have arisen. I have fielded several consistent requests
from our residents and staff.

1. We understand the maximum allowable height of new developments is 55 feet. However,
as exemplified by The Gramercy, at 555 Laurel Avenue, elevator shafts and other rooftop
additions often impact views further than the 55 feet. Therefore, we request that the
development be changed from five stories to four stories.

2. We believe that an important part of the planning process is to ensure that the
landscaping around the building is esthetically pleasing. We believe that it is equally
important that the view of the building's rooftop from nearby buildings of the same or
greater height be esthetically pleasing. Therefore, we would respectfully ask that the
design of the rooftop involve a qualified landscape architect, with the goal of attractively
screening off any mechanical components on the roof from view by including some
greenery that would enhance the view from the higher floors of nearby buildings. We
recognize that this would need to be anticipated early in the development project so we
are sharing our request now. We offer and invite collaboration with this architect to
ensure that this project enhances rather than detracts from our esthetic experience.

3. Additionally, we request that 1.5 parking spots be built to accommodate every apartment
in the development at a minimum. Parking in the neighborhood is already impacted and
the addition of such a large development will further increase this problem.

Thank you for your time and consideration. We look forward to your response
All the best,

Camille Christie, Executive Director
The Stratford

601 Laurel Avenue | San Mateo, CA 94401 | p. 650-342-4106
TheStratfordSM.com

From: John Hershberger

Subject: Nazareth Vista Development 
 
To San Mateo Planning Commission 
I live in the Gramercy on the Park condominiums directly across 6th Avenue from the proposed Nazareth Vista 
Development.  I, along with many of my neighbors in the Gramercy, have a number of concerns about the proposed 
development, but I’ll focus on just two for now. 
 1.      If I understand correctly, Dinar and Associates has requested an exemption to the City’s 20‐foot setback 
requirement, and plans to extend the building all the way out to the sidewalk.  We also understand the building design 
includes an entrance for retail parking on 6th Avenue, suggesting that there will be a constant flow of traffic coming in 
and out of the garage all day and possibly in the evening as well.  
 2.     The trash room for the entire building opens onto 6th Avenue.  With an exemption of the set‐back requirement the 
dumpsters there will create unavoidable congestion out into the street on 6th Avenue during their twice‐weekly pickups 
for trash and once‐a‐week pickup for recycling.  The noise and congestion of rolling dumpsters and trucks picking up and 
dropping off dumpsters would be a major source of irritation for those who live nearby. The combination of not having a 
setback and having all trash and recycling being dealt with on 6th Avenue really is unacceptable from our point of view. 
We urge the Planning Commission to deny Dinar’s request for a set‐back exemption and ask Dinar and Associates to 
reconsider where retail parking and trash collection and recycling take place.  Thank you for your consideration. 
John Hershberger 
555 Laurel Avenue, 
 
San Mateo, CA 94401

from the sidewalks. Both factors affect the appearance of our fair city and its 
appeal as a town with open light and open feel for the residents. 
It especially affects our building and threatens to undermine our current value. 
B St. is a commercial zone. The encroachment of this large building and no setback 
will likely negatively affect the continued attempt to develop this area for services 
to our town. 
  
The extra‐large building and encroachment of the sidewalks will have the effect of 
blocking light, views, and open space for neighboring building residents. The 
buildings in place now have all had to adhere to city planning codes of height 
limitations and setbacks. There was a reason at that time to require height 
restrictions and setbacks which have not changed!

existing neighborhood. This traffic endangers the elderly and disabled people, who 
are in large numbers, in the neighboring buildings as they use sidewalks. The lack 
of setback makes automobile and truck traffic more difficult to see coming and 
vice‐versa.

john@johncarnes.com
Cc:
Somer Smith; Planning Commission
Subject:
Re: Nazareth Vista Comments
 
Sent from my iPhone 
 
 
On Feb 4, 2022, at 2:16 PM, 
wrote: 
 
To: Somer Smith and the Planning Commission of the City of San Mateo 
  
I write to you with deep concern about the project being proposed in San Mateo on B Street between 
6th and 7th Avenues called Nazareth Vista. As a resident of Gramercy on the Park across 6th Avenue from 
the property, this project has a number of issues that I find disturbing: 
  
1. Traffic: There are two parking entrances to the garages. On 7th Avenue is the entrance to the 
ramp to the lower, underground garage that will be used by residents. On 6th Avenue is the 
entrance to the ground level garage that will be used by retail shoppers and visitors to the 
building. The 6th Avenue parking entrance is the busy one that will be used all day for transient 
vehicles and, if Vista follows the parking rules/setup as have other lots being approved, it will 
allow public parking during hours when retail is not open. This level of constant traffic is not 
acceptable. 
  
2. Trash and recycling: The trash room for the Vista complex opens onto 6th Avenue. This means 
that dumpsters and trash containers will litter the sidewalks and/or street on two trash 
collection days and one recycling collection day. Since these containers are likely to be put out 
the day before pickup, that gives us six days a week with dumpsters with which to contend. 6th 
Avenue is not built for that type of activity without causing considerable disruption. 
  
3. Building setback: There is an exception request for the Nazareth Vista to forego the required 20‐
foot setback of the neighborhood. This means the building will encroach on our open space and 
block significantly more light than it would with the setback in place. This is unacceptable as it 
will change the character of the neighborhood. 
  
In reviewing the plans, it is painfully obvious that quite a few liberties were taken with this building that 
other projects have not. Although I realize that progress is inevitable and that new buildings must be 
larger to justify the costs of land and construction, it is absolutely vital that these new structures 
conform to the codes in place and blend into the existing neighborhood where they will live for decades. 
  
Thank you for your consideration of these matters. 
  
John Carnes 
__________ 
John Carnes

To: Somer Smith and the Planning Commission of the City of San Mateo 
  
I write to you with deep concern about the project being proposed in San Mateo on B 
Street between 6th and 7th Avenues called Nazareth Vista. As a resident of Gramercy on 
the Park across 6th Avenue from the property, this project has a number of issues that I 
find disturbing: 
  
1. Traffic: There are two parking entrances to the garages. On 7th Avenue is the 
entrance to the ramp to the lower, underground garage that will be used by 
residents. On 6th Avenue is the entrance to the ground level garage that will be 
used by retail shoppers and visitors to the building. The 6th Avenue parking 
entrance is the busy one that will be used all day for transient vehicles and, if 
Vista follows the parking rules/setup as have other lots being approved, it will 
allow public parking during hours when retail is not open. This level of constant 
traffic is not acceptable. 
  
2. Trash and recycling: The trash room for the Vista complex opens onto 
6th Avenue. This means that dumpsters and trash containers will litter the 
sidewalks and/or street on two trash collection days and one recycling collection 
day. Since these containers are likely to be put out the day before pickup, that 
gives us six days a week with dumpsters with which to contend. 6th Avenue is 
not built for that type of activity without causing considerable disruption. 
  
3. Building setback: There is an exception request for the Nazareth Vista to forego 
the required 20‐foot setback of the neighborhood. This means the building will 
encroach on our open space and block significantly more light than it would 
with the setback in place. This is unacceptable as it will change the character of 
the neighborhood. 
  
In reviewing the plans, it is painfully obvious that quite a few liberties were taken with 
this building that other projects have not. Although I realize that progress is inevitable 
and that new buildings must be larger to justify the costs of land and construction, it is 
absolutely vital that these new structures conform to the codes in place and blend into 
the existing neighborhood where they will live for decades. 
  
Thank you for your consideration of these matters. 
 
Ronald Hwang DMD

PA-2021-036  616 South B St Nazareth Vista Pre-Application
Hi Somer,  
 
My name is Rick Onorato, I own a small building at 611 South B directly accross the street from the proposed Nazareth 
Vista project. I attended the zoom meeting on January 20th and was overwhelmed by the enormity of this project. Of 
course there are taller buildings behind this, but this would be the tallest on B Street and it will literally leave surrounding 
buildings in it's shadow for most of the day. 
 
On the plus side I think it has a clean modern look but I would like to see it scaled down. Could it have both parking levels 
below grade making it a more acceptable four-story building?  Maybe it could have more of a setback from the street 
allowing for more greenscape. 
 
I would appreciate it if my questions could be addressed at future meetings as I know I am not the only neighboring 
building owner that has concerns about the size of this. 
 
Thank you, 
 
Rick Onorato 
South B Street Properties IV, LLC 
 
Menlo Park, CA 94026

Subject:
Nazareth Vista Project
Dear Somer, 
 
I am the owner of the mixed use office and retail building at 301 S Bst, as well as the office building at 77 N San Mateo 
Dr in San Mateo. I am in favor of the Nazareth Vista project that is being considered by the City at this time.  Our local 
area needs to step forward to keep pace with the flow of business outward from downtown San Mateo.  The area has 
been outmoded, and new fresh developments would be very welcome.  I work, walk and drive along B Street, and the 
two existing Nazareth developments at 7th and 8th Street have always proven to be the most visually appealing and 
welcoming buildings on the street.  The planter boxes with flowers and shrubs, the trees surrounding these buildings, 
and the well maintained street frontages provide much enjoyment in our neighborhood.  I fully expect that the proposed 
Nazareth Vista project will bring the same vitality to the area, with a pleasant street frontage as shown in the drawings 
you sent out.  I support this proposed development wholeheartedly. 
 
Sincerely,  
 
Les Keyak

Cc:
Planning
Subject:
Nazareth Vista 616 South B St. Proposals
  
Dear Planning Commissioners, 
 
There are a number of issues and concerns shared by many fellow owners at the Gramercy. I personally would
like to focus on the waivers being considered for the subject, particularly the setback requirement. 
 
Waivers are necessary for flexibility and occasionally to achieve unusually positive trade offs. However, 
discipline to limit them is important for any well planned cities to continue to thrive.  
 
San Mateo is the 11th city of various population sizes, which my family has lived in, around the world. 
 
We had chosen San Mateo as our home for retirement because we are attracted by its beauty and character, 
and the promise that both would continue. As a business executive, I expect continual development, and would 
hope that they will add to the economic vitality without degrading any of its fine character. 
 
However, we are concerned that the waiver on the setbacks will incur a major cost without the offsetting 
benefits. The waiver would also be incongruent (not aligned) with the residential buildings on the 6th and the 
7th Avenue. I also wonder what would happen to the 5 trees on the 6th Avenue neighboring Stratbally without 
the normal setback. 
 
In short, the reputation of San Mateo and the Planning Commission may be at stake here. I therefore hope that 
you dedicate time in your deliberations on the waivers, particularly on the setback. 
 
Thank you for your consideration. 
 
 
Boon Kang  
Owner and a Director at the Gramercy On the Park HOA Board  
(however, not representing the Board in any way) 
 
555 Laurel Ave, 
 
San Mateo CA 94401
